      </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         \xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Density\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         1,733/km\n         <sup>\n          2\n         </sup>\n         (4,488/sq\xc2\xa0mi)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         \xe2\x80\xa2\n         <a UTC-5\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n          \xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0Summer         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">\n          ZIP code\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td class="adr">\n         <span class="postal-code">\n          23501-23515, 23517-23521, 23523, 23529, 23541, 23551\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">\n          Area code(s)\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Area_code_757" title="Area code 757">\n          757\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedrow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a 51-57000\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_1-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR2-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr ID\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         1497051\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR3_2-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-GR3-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr class="mergedtoprow">\n        <th scope="row">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <span class="url">\n          <a class="external text" href="http://www.norfolk.gov/" rel="nofollow">\n           www\n           <wbr/>\n           .norfolk\n           <wbr/>\n           .gov\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Norfolk\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">\n            n\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: \'ar\' in \'war\'">\n            \xc9\x94\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">\n            f\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xca\x8a/: \'oo\' in \'foot\'">\n            \xca\x8a\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">\n        <small title="English pronunciation respelling">\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           NOR\n          </b>\n          -fuuk\n         </i>\n        </small>\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <small>\n         locally\n        </small>\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">\n            n\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x92/: \'o\' in \'body\'">\n            \xc9\x92\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">\n            f\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xca\x8a/: \'oo\' in \'foot\'">\n            \xca\x8a\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">\n        <small title="English pronunciation respelling">\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           NOF\n          </b>\n          -uuk\n         </i>\n        </small>\n       </a>\n       ) is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Independent_city_(United_States)" title="Independent city (United States)">\n        independent city\n       </a>\n       located in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">\n        Commonwealth\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . At the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 census\n       </a>\n       , the population was 242,803;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-QF-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in 2015, the population was estimated to be 247,189\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       making it the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Virginia" title="List of cities in Virginia">\n        second-most populous city in Virginia\n       </a>\n       after neighboring\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk is located at the core of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       metropolitan area, named for the large\n       <a href="/wiki/Harbor" title="Harbor">\n        natural harbor\n       </a>\n       of the same name located at the mouth of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       . It is one of nine cities and seven counties that constitute the Hampton Roads metro area, officially known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach-Norfolk-Newport_News,_VA-NC_MSA" title="Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA">\n        Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA\n       </a>\n       . The city is bordered to the west by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">\n        Elizabeth River\n       </a>\n       and to the north by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       . It also shares land borders with the independent cities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n        Chesapeake\n       </a>\n       to its south and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach" title="Virginia Beach">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       to its east. Norfolk is one of the oldest cities in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       , and is considered to be the historic, urban, financial, and cultural center of the region.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city has a long history as a strategic military and transportation point. The largest Navy base in the world,\n       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Station_Norfolk" title="Naval Station Norfolk">\n        Naval Station Norfolk\n       </a>\n       , is located in Norfolk along with one of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">\n        NATO\'s\n       </a>\n       two\n       <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Transformation" title="Allied Command Transformation">\n        Strategic Command headquarters\n       </a>\n       . The city also has the corporate headquarters of\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">\n        Norfolk Southern Railway\n       </a>\n       , one of North America\'s principal\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">\n        Class I railroads\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A._P._Moller-Maersk_Group#Maersk_Line.2C_Limited" title="A. P. Moller-Maersk Group">\n        Maersk Line, Limited\n       </a>\n       , which manages the world\'s largest fleet of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flag_State" title="Flag State">\n        US-flag vessels\n       </a>\n       . As the city is bordered by multiple bodies of water, Norfolk has many miles of riverfront and bayfront property, including beaches on the Chesapeake Bay. It is linked to its neighbors by an extensive network of\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate highways\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bridge" title="Bridge">\n        bridges\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tunnel" title="Tunnel">\n        tunnels\n       </a>\n       , and three\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridge-tunnel" title="Bridge-tunnel">\n        bridge-tunnel\n       </a>\n       complexes, which are the only bridge-tunnels in the United States.\n      </p>\n </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           15\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1     </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           17\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Norfolk,_Virginia" title="History of Norfolk, Virginia">\n        History of Norfolk, Virginia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Timeline of Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Timeline of Norfolk, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_years">\n        Colonial years\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colonial years">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 1619, the Governor of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Colony" title="Virginia Colony">\n        Virginia Colony\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Yeardley" title="George Yeardley">\n        Sir George Yeardley\n       </a>\n       incorporated four jurisdictions, termed\n       <i>\n        citties,\n       </i>\n       for the developed portion of the colony. These formed the basis for colonial representative government in the newly minted\n       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Burgesses" title="House of Burgesses">\n        House of Burgesses\n       </a>\n       . What would become Norfolk was put under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City_(Virginia_Company)" title="Elizabeth City (Virginia Company)">\n        Elizabeth Cittie\n       </a>\n       incorporation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1634\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">\n        King Charles I\n       </a>\n       reorganized the colony into a system of\n       <a href="/wiki/Shires_of_Virginia" title="Shires of Virginia">\n        shires\n       </a>\n       . The former\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City_(Virginia_Company)" title="Elizabeth City (Virginia Company)">\n        Elizabeth Cittie\n       </a>\n       became\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City_Shire" title="Elizabeth City Shire">\n        Elizabeth City Shire\n       </a>\n       . After persuading 105 people to settle in the colony,\n       <a href="/wiki/Adam_Thoroughgood" title="Adam Thoroughgood">\n        Adam Thoroughgood\n       </a>\n       (who had immigrated to Virginia in 1622 from\n       <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Lynn" title="King\'s Lynn">\n        King\'s Lynn\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">\n        England\n       </a>\n       ) was granted a large land holding, through the head rights system, along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lynnhaven_River" title="Lynnhaven River">\n        Lynnhaven River\n       </a>\n       in 1636.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Hampton_Roads" title="South Hampton Roads">\n        South Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       portion of the shire was separated, Thoroughgood suggested the name of his birthplace for the newly formed\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Norfolk_County,_Virginia" title="New Norfolk County, Virginia">\n        New Norfolk County\n       </a>\n       . One year later, it was split into two counties,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upper_Norfolk_County" title="Upper Norfolk County">\n        Upper Norfolk\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Norfolk_County,_Virginia" title="Lower Norfolk County, Virginia">\n        Lower Norfolk\n       </a>\n       (the latter is incorporated within present-day City of Norfolk), chiefly on Thoroughgood\'s recommendation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_History_Chapter_4_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_History_Chapter_4-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This area of Virginia became known as the place of entrepreneurs, including men of the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Company" title="London Company">\n        Virginia Company of London\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk developed in the late-seventeenth century as a "Half Moone" fort was constructed and 50 acres (200,000\xc2\xa0m\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) were acquired from local natives of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Powhatan_Confederacy" title="Powhatan Confederacy">\n        Powhatan Confederacy\n       </a>\n       in exchange for 10,000 pounds of tobacco. The House of Burgesses established the "Towne of Lower Norfolk County" in 1680.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_History_Chapter_6_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_History_Chapter_6-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_History_Chapter_7_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_History_Chapter_7-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1691, a final county subdivision took place when Lower Norfolk County split to form\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_County,_Virginia" title="Norfolk County, Virginia">\n        Norfolk County\n       </a>\n       (included in present-day cities of Norfolk, Chesapeake, and parts of Portsmouth) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Anne_County" title="Princess Anne County">\n        Princess Anne County\n       </a>\n       (present-day City of Virginia Beach).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk was incorporated in 1705. In 1730, a tobacco inspection site was located here. According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Inspection_Act" title="Tobacco Inspection Act">\n        Tobacco Inspection Act\n       </a>\n       , the inspection was\n       <i>\n        "At Norfolk Town, upon the fort land, in the County of Norfolk; and\n        <a href="/wiki/Kempsville,_Virginia" title="Kempsville, Virginia">\n         Kemp\'s Landing\n        </a>\n        , in Princess Anne, under one inspection."\n       </i>\n       In 1736\n       <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">\n        George II\n       </a>\n       granted it a royal charter as a borough.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_History_Chapter_9_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_History_Chapter_9-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 1775, Norfolk developed into what contemporary observers argued was the most prosperous city in Virginia. It was an important port for exporting goods to the British Isles and beyond. In part because of its merchants\' numerous trading ties with other parts of the British Empire, Norfolk served as a strong base of\n       <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">\n        Loyalist\n       </a>\n       support during the early part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       . After fleeing the colonial capital of\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Dunmore" title="Earl of Dunmore">\n        Lord Dunmore\n       </a>\n       , the Royal Governor of Virginia, tried to reestablish control of the colony from Norfolk. Dunmore secured small victories at Norfolk but was forced into exile by the American rebels, commanded by\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Woodford" title="William Woodford">\n        Colonel Woodford\n       </a>\n       . His departure brought an end to more than 168 years of British colonial rule in Virginia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_from_Colonial_Williamsburg_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-History_from_Colonial_Williamsburg-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On New Year\'s Day, 1776, Lord Dunmore\'s fleet of three ships shelled the city of Norfolk for more than eight hours. The damage from the shells and fires started by the British and spread by the patriots destroyed over 800 buildings, almost two-thirds of the city. The patriots destroyed the remaining buildings for strategic reasons in February.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Only the walls of\n       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul%27s_Episcopal_Church_(Norfolk,_Virginia)" title="Saint Paul\'s Episcopal Church (Norfolk, Virginia)">\n        Saint Paul\'s Episcopal Church\n       </a>\n       survived the bombardment and subsequent fires. A cannonball from the bombardment (fired by the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/HMS_Liverpool_(1758)" title="HMS Liverpool (1758)">\n         Liverpool\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ) remains within the wall of Saint Paul\'s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HMS_Otter_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HMS_Otter-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nineteenth_century">\n        Nineteenth century\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Nineteenth century">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norfolk,_from_Gosport,_Virginia_(NYPL_b12349153-423885).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3192" data-file-width="4768" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg/220px-Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg/330px-Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg/440px-Norfolk%2C_from_Gosport%2C_Virginia_%28NYPL_b12349153-423885%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Norfolk,_from_Gosport,_Virginia_(NYPL_b12349153-423885).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Norfolk, from Gosport, Virginia\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <a class="external text" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/File:Norfolk,_from_Gosport,_Virginia_(NYPL_b12349153-423885).jpg">\n          New York Public Library\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="500" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg/170px-Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg/255px-Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg/340px-Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cannonball_lodged_in_church_wall.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Where one of Lord Dunmore\'s shells landed during the American Revolutionary War\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="493" data-file-width="338" height="248" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg/170px-Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg/255px-Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cd/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts" title="Joseph Jenkins Roberts">\n          Joseph Jenkins Roberts\n         </a>\n         , born and raised in Norfolk, became the first President of\n         <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">\n          Liberia\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Following recovery from the Revolutionary War\'s burning, Norfolk and her citizens struggled to rebuild. In 1804, another serious fire along the city\'s waterfront destroyed some 300 buildings and the city suffered a serious economic setback. During the 1820s, agrarian communities across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        American South\n       </a>\n       suffered a prolonged recession, which caused many families to migrate to other areas. Many moved west into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">\n        Piedmont\n       </a>\n       , or further into\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">\n        Tennessee\n       </a>\n       . Such migration also followed the exhaustion of soil due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">\n        tobacco\n       </a>\n       cultivation in the Tidewater, where it had been the primary commodity crop for generations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Virginia made some attempts to phase out\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">\n        slavery\n       </a>\n       , and manumissions had increased in the first two decades after the war.\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson_Randolph" title="Thomas Jefferson Randolph">\n        Thomas Jefferson Randolph\n       </a>\n       gained passage of an 1832 resolution for gradual abolition in the state, but by that time, increased demand from development in the Deep South created a large internal market for slavery. The invention of the cotton gin in the late-eighteenth century had enabled the profitable cultivation of short-staple cotton in the uplands, which was widely used.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">\n        American Colonization Society\n       </a>\n       proposed to "\n       <a href="/wiki/Back-to-Africa_movement" title="Back-to-Africa movement">\n        repatriate\n       </a>\n       " free blacks and freed slaves to Africa by establishing the new colony of Liberia and paying for transportation. But most African-Americans wanted to stay in their birthplace of the United States and achieve freedom and rights there. For a period, many emigrants to Liberia from Virginia and\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">\n        North Carolina\n       </a>\n       embarked from the port of Norfolk.\n       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Jenkins_Roberts" title="Joseph Jenkins Roberts">\n        Joseph Jenkins Roberts\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_person_of_color" title="Free person of color">\n        free person of color\n       </a>\n       native to Norfolk, emigrated via the American Colonization Society and later was elected as the first president of\n       <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">\n        Liberia\n       </a>\n       , establishing a powerful family.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Roberts-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On June 7, 1855, the 183-ft. vessel\n       <i>\n        Benjamin Franklin\n       </i>\n       put into Hampton Roads for repairs. She had just sailed from the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">\n        West Indies\n       </a>\n       where there had been an outbreak of\n       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">\n        yellow fever\n       </a>\n       . The port health officer ordered the ship quarantined. After eleven days, a second inspection found no issues, so she was allowed to dock. A few days later, the first cases of yellow fever were discovered in Norfolk, and a machinist died from the disease on July 8. By August, several people were dying per day, and a third of the city\'s population had fled in the hopes of escaping the epidemic. No one understood how the disease was transmitted. With both Norfolk and Portsmouth being infected, New York banned all traffic from those sites. Neighboring cities also banned residents from Norfolk. The epidemic spread through the city via mosquitoes and poor sanitation, affecting every family and causing widespread panic. The number of infected reached 5,000 in September, and by the second week, 1,500 had died in Norfolk and Portsmouth. As the weather cooled, the outbreak began to wane, leaving a final tally of about 3,200 dead.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It took the city some time to recover.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In early 1861, Norfolk voters instructed their delegate to vote for secession. Virginia voted to secede from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       . In the spring of 1862, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads" title="Battle of Hampton Roads">\n        Battle of Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       took place off the northwest shore of the city\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point Peninsula\n       </a>\n       , marking the first fight between two\n       <a href="/wiki/Ironclad_warship" title="Ironclad warship">\n        ironclads\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">\n        USS\n        <i>\n         Monitor\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/CSS_Virginia" title="CSS Virginia">\n        CSS\n        <i>\n         Virginia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       . The battle ended in a stalemate, but changed the course of naval warfare; from then on,\n       <a href="/wiki/Warship" title="Warship">\n        warships\n       </a>\n       were fortified with metal.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monitor-Merrimac_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Monitor-Merrimac-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In May 1862, Norfolk Mayor William Lamb surrendered the city to Union\n       <a href="/wiki/General_(United_States)" title="General (United States)">\n        General\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/John_E._Wool" title="John E. Wool">\n        John E. Wool\n       </a>\n       and his forces. They held the city under\n       <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">\n        martial law\n       </a>\n       for the duration of the Civil War. Thousands of slaves from the region escaped to Union lines to gain freedom; they quickly set up schools in Norfolk to start learning how to read and write, years before the end of the war.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk_History_Chapter_46_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk_History_Chapter_46-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_to_present">\n        20th century to present\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 20th century to present">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       1907 brought both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginian_Railway" title="Virginian Railway">\n        Virginian Railway\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Jamestown_Exposition" title="Jamestown Exposition">\n        Jamestown Exposition\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Sewell%27s_Point" title="Sewell\'s Point">\n        Sewell\'s Point\n       </a>\n       . The large\n       <a href="/wiki/Naval_Review" title="Naval Review">\n        Naval Review\n       </a>\n       at the Exposition demonstrated the peninsula\'s favorable location and laid the groundwork for the world\'s largest naval base. Southern Democrats in Congress gained its location here. Commemorating the tricentennial anniversary of the founding of Jamestown, the exposition featured many prominent officials, including President\n       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">\n        Theodore Roosevelt\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Congress" title="Member of Congress">\n        members of Congress\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">\n        diplomats\n       </a>\n       from twenty-one countries. By 1917, as the US prepared to enter\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">\n        World War I\n       </a>\n       , the Naval Air Station Hampton Roads had been constructed on the former exposition grounds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jamestown_Exposition_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jamestown_Exposition-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the first half of the twentieth century, the city of Norfolk expanded its borders through annexation. In 1906, the city annexed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Incorporated_town" title="Incorporated town">\n        incorporated town\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkley,_Virginia" title="Berkley, Virginia">\n        Berkley\n       </a>\n       , making the city cross the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">\n        Elizabeth River\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk:_1906_Annexation_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk:_1906_Annexation-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1923, the city expanded to include Sewell\'s Point,\n       <a href="/wiki/Willoughby_Spit" title="Willoughby Spit">\n        Willoughby Spit\n       </a>\n       , the town of Campostella, and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_View,_Virginia" title="Ocean View, Virginia">\n        Ocean View\n       </a>\n       area. The city included the Navy Base and miles of beach property fronting on\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk:_1923_Annexation_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk:_1923_Annexation-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After a smaller annexation in 1959, and a 1988 land swap with\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       , the city assumed its current boundaries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norfolk:_1955_Annexation_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Norfolk:_1955_Annexation-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With the dawn of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate Highway System\n       </a>\n       following World War II, new highways were constructed in the region. A series of bridges and tunnels, constructed during fifteen years, linked Norfolk with\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">\n        the Peninsula\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n        Portsmouth\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       . In 1952, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Tunnel" title="Downtown Tunnel">\n        Downtown Tunnel\n       </a>\n       opened to connect Norfolk with the city of Portsmouth. The highways also stimulated the development of new housing suburbs, leading to the population spreading out. Additional bridges and tunnels included the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads_Bridge-Tunnel" title="Hampton Roads Bridge-Tunnel">\n        Hampton Roads Bridge-Tunnel\n       </a>\n       in 1957,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hampton_Roads_Bridge_Tunnel_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hampton_Roads_Bridge_Tunnel-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Tunnel_(Virginia)" title="Midtown Tunnel (Virginia)">\n        Midtown Tunnel\n       </a>\n       in 1962,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Midtown_Tunnel_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Midtown_Tunnel-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach-Norfolk_Expressway" title="Virginia Beach-Norfolk Expressway">\n        Virginia Beach-Norfolk Expressway\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_264_(Virginia)" title="Interstate 264 (Virginia)">\n        Interstate 264\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Route_44_(Virginia_1980s)" title="State Route 44 (Virginia 1980s)">\n        State Route 44\n       </a>\n       ) in 1967.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interstate_264_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Interstate_264-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1991, the new\n       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Tunnel" title="Downtown Tunnel">\n        Downtown Tunnel\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkley_Bridge_(Virginia)" title="Berkley Bridge (Virginia)">\n        Berkley Bridge\n       </a>\n       complex opened a new system of multiple lanes of highway and interchanges connecting Downtown Norfolk and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_464" title="Interstate 464">\n        Interstate 464\n       </a>\n       with the Downtown Tunnel tubes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Downtown_Tunnel_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Downtown_Tunnel-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1954 the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court\n       </a>\n       ruled in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">\n         Brown v. Board of Education\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       that\n       <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">\n        segregated\n       </a>\n       public schools were\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unconstitutional" title="Unconstitutional">\n        unconstitutional\n       </a>\n       , as the public system was supported by all taxpayers. It ordered\n       <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">\n        integration\n       </a>\n       , but Virginia pursued a policy of "\n       <a href="/wiki/Massive_resistance" title="Massive resistance">\n        massive resistance\n       </a>\n       ". (At this time, most black citizens were still\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disfranchisement_after_Reconstruction_era" title="Disfranchisement after Reconstruction era">\n        disfranchised\n       </a>\n       under the state\'s turn-of-the-century constitution and discriminatory practices related to voter registration and elections.) The\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">\n        Virginia General Assembly\n       </a>\n       prohibited state funding for integrated public schools.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1958,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">\n        United States district courts\n       </a>\n       in Virginia ordered schools to open for the first time on a racially integrated basis. In response,\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Virginia" title="Governor of Virginia">\n        Governor\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Lindsay_Almond,_Jr." title="James Lindsay Almond, Jr.">\n        James Lindsay Almond, Jr.\n       </a>\n       ordered the schools closed. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Supreme_Court_of_Appeals" title="Virginia Supreme Court of Appeals">\n        Virginia Supreme Court of Appeals\n       </a>\n       declared the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_law" title="State law">\n        state law\n       </a>\n       to be in conflict with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Virginia" title="Constitution of Virginia">\n        state constitution\n       </a>\n       and ordered all public schools to be funded, whether integrated or not. About ten days later, Almond capitulated and asked the General Assembly to rescind several "massive resistance" laws.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Massive_Resistance_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Massive_Resistance-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In September 1959, seventeen black children entered six previously segregated Norfolk public schools.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Virginian-Pilot" title="The Virginian-Pilot">\n         Virginian-Pilot\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       editor\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenoir_Chambers" title="Lenoir Chambers">\n        Lenoir Chambers\n       </a>\n       editorialized against massive resistance and earned the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_Editorial_Writing" title="Pulitzer Prize for Editorial Writing">\n        Pulitzer Prize for Editorial Writing\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lenoir_Chambers_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lenoir_Chambers-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       With new\n       <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">\n        suburban\n       </a>\n       developments beckoning, many white middle-class residents\n       <a href="/wiki/White_flight" title="White flight">\n        moved out of the city\n       </a>\n       along new highway routes, and Norfolk\'s population declined, a pattern repeated in numerous cities during the postwar era independently of segregation issues. In the late-1960s and early-1970s, the advent of newer suburban shopping destinations along with freeways spelled demise for the fortunes of downtown\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Granby_Street" title="Granby Street">\n        Granby Street\n       </a>\n       commercial corridor, located just a few blocks inland from the waterfront. The opening of malls and large shopping centers drew off retail business from Granby Street.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JANAF_History_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-JANAF_History-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk\'s city leaders began a long push to\n       <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">\n        revive its urban core\n       </a>\n       . While Granby Street underwent decline, Norfolk city leaders focused on the waterfront and its collection of decaying piers and warehouses. Many obsolete shipping and warehousing facilities were demolished. In their place, planners created a new boulevard, Waterside Drive, along which many of the high-rise buildings in Norfolk\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Skyline" title="Skyline">\n        skyline\n       </a>\n       have been erected. In 1983, the city and\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Rouse_Company" title="The Rouse Company">\n        The Rouse Company\n       </a>\n       developed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Waterside_(Norfolk,_Virginia)" title="Waterside (Norfolk, Virginia)">\n        Waterside\n       </a>\n       festival marketplace to attract people back to the waterfront and catalyze further downtown redevelopment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waterside_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Waterside-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other facilities opened in the ensuing years, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Harbor_Park" title="Harbor Park">\n        Harbor Park\n       </a>\n       baseball stadium, home of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Tides" title="Norfolk Tides">\n        Norfolk Tides\n       </a>\n       Triple-A\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" title="Minor league baseball">\n        minor league baseball\n       </a>\n       team. In 1995, the park was named the finest facility in minor league baseball by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Baseball_America" title="Baseball America">\n         Baseball America\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harbor_Park_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Harbor_Park-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Norfolk\'s efforts to revitalize its downtown have attracted acclaim from economic development and urban planning circles throughout the country. Downtown\'s rising fortunes helped to expand the city\'s revenues and allowed the city to direct attention to other neighborhoods.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_Norfolk_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_Norfolk-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="631" data-file-width="639" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg/200px-Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg/300px-Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg/400px-Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Newport_news_norfolk_portsmouth.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n          Newport News\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n          Hampton\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_County,_Virginia" title="Isle of Wight County, Virginia">\n          Isle of Wight County\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n          Suffolk\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n          Chesapeake\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n          Portsmouth\n         </a>\n         and Norfolk,\n         <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n          Virginia\n         </a>\n         from space, July 1996. Norfolk is located in the upper right quadrant, and east is at the top.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city has a total area of 96 square miles (250\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), of which 54 square miles (140\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is land and 42 square miles (110\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) (43.9%) is water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR1-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Norfolk is located at\n       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">\n        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;params=36_55_N_76_12_W_type:city">\n         <span class="geo-default">\n          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           <span class="latitude">\n            36\xc2\xb055\xe2\x80\xb2N\n           </span>\n           <span class="longitude">\n            76\xc2\xb012\xe2\x80\xb2W\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-multi-punct">\n          \xef\xbb\xbf / \xef\xbb\xbf\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-nondefault">\n          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           36.917\xc2\xb0N 76.200\xc2\xb0W\n          </span>\n          <span style="display:none">\n           \xef\xbb\xbf /\n           <span class="geo">\n            36.917; -76.200\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       (36.8857\xc2\xb0 N, 76.2599\xc2\xb0 W)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city is located at the southeastern corner of\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       at the junction of the Elizabeth River and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       . The Hampton Roads\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_metropolitan_area" title="United States metropolitan area">\n        Metropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       (officially known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach-Norfolk-Newport_News,_VA-NC_MSA" title="Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA">\n        Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA\n       </a>\n       ) is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas">\n        37th largest\n       </a>\n       in the United States, with an estimated population of 1,716,624 in 2014. The area includes the Virginia cities of Norfolk,\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Beach,_Virginia" title="Virginia Beach, Virginia">\n        Virginia Beach\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake,_Virginia" title="Chesapeake, Virginia">\n        Chesapeake\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">\n        Hampton\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Poquoson,_Virginia" title="Poquoson, Virginia">\n        Poquoson\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth,_Virginia" title="Portsmouth, Virginia">\n        Portsmouth\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Suffolk,_Virginia" title="Suffolk, Virginia">\n        Suffolk\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       , and the counties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gloucester_County,_Virginia" title="Gloucester County, Virginia">\n        Gloucester\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_County,_Virginia" title="Isle of Wight County, Virginia">\n        Isle of Wight\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/James_City_County,_Virginia" title="James City County, Virginia">\n        James City\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mathews_County,_Virginia" title="Mathews County, Virginia">\n        Mathews\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/York_County,_Virginia" title="York County, Virginia">\n        York\n       </a>\n       , as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">\n        North Carolina\n       </a>\n       counties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Currituck_County,_North_Carolina" title="Currituck County, North Carolina">\n        Currituck\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gates_County,_North_Carolina" title="Gates County, North Carolina">\n        Gates\n       </a>\n       . The city of Norfolk is recognized as the central business district, while the Virginia Beach oceanside resort district and\n       <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">\n        Williamsburg\n       </a>\n       are primarily centers of tourism. Virginia Beach is the most populated city within the MSA though it functions more as a suburb. Additionally, Norfolk is part of the Virginia Beach-Norfolk, VA-NC\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">\n        Combined Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       , which includes the Virginia Beach-Norfolk-Newport News, VA-NC MSA, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_City,_North_Carolina_Micropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Elizabeth City, North Carolina Micropolitan Statistical Area">\n        Elizabeth City, North Carolina Micropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kill_Devil_Hills,_NC" title="Kill Devil Hills, NC">\n        Kill Devil Hills, NC\n       </a>\n       Micropolitan Statistical Area. The CSA is the 32nd largest in the nation with an estimated population in 2013 of 1,810,266.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to extensive riverfront property, Norfolk has miles of bayfront resort property and beaches in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Willoughby_Spit" title="Willoughby Spit">\n        Willoughby Spit\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_View,_Virginia" title="Ocean View, Virginia">\n        Ocean View\n       </a>\n       communities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Being low-lying and largely surrounded by water, Norfolk is particularly vulnerable to rising sea levels. In addition, the land on which it is built is slowly subsiding. Some areas already flood regularly at high tide, and the city commissioned a study in 2012 to investigate how to address the issue in the future: it reported the cost of dealing with a sea-level rise of one foot would be around $1,000,000,000. Since then, scientists at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Institute_of_Marine_Science" title="Virginia Institute of Marine Science">\n        Virginia Institute of Marine Science\n       </a>\n       in 2013 have estimated that if current trends hold, the sea in Norfolk will rise by 5 and 1/2 feet or more by the end of this century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">\n        Cityscape\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cityscape">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Norfolk,_Virginia" title="List of tallest buildings in Norfolk, Virginia">\n        List of tallest buildings in Norfolk, Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norfolk,_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg/300px-Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg/450px-Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg/600px-Norfolk%2C_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Norfolk,_Virginia_skyline_2016.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Norfolk, Virginia skyline from across the\n         <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_River_(Virginia)" title="Elizabeth River (Virginia)">\n          Elizabeth River\n         </a>\n         in 2016\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:133px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ghent_neighborhood_house,_Norfolk,_VA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="203" data-file-width="131" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Ghent_neighborhood_house%2C_Norfolk%2C_VA.jpg" width="131"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ghent_neighborhood_house,_Norfolk,_VA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A home in the Ghent neighborhood\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When Norfolk was first settled, homes were made of wood and\n       <a href="/wiki/Framing_(construction)" title="Framing (construction)">\n        frame\n       </a>\n       construction, similar to most medieval English-style homes. These homes had wide\n       <a href="/wiki/Chimney" title="Chimney">\n        chimneys\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thatching" title="Thatching">\n        thatch roofs\n       </a>\n       . Some decades after the town was first laid out in 1682, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">\n        Georgian architectural style\n       </a>\n       , which was popular in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        South\n       </a>\n       at the time, was used.\n       <a href="/wiki/Brick" title="Brick">\n        Brick\n       </a>\n       was considered more substantial construction; patterns were made by brick laid and Flemish bond. This style evolved to include projecting center pavilions,\n       <a href="/wiki/Palladian_architecture" title="Palladian architecture">\n        Palladian\n       </a>\n       windows,\n       <a href="/wiki/Baluster" title="Baluster">\n        balustraded\n       </a>\n       roof decks, and two-story\n       <a href="/wiki/Portico" title="Portico">\n        porticoes\n       </a>\n       . By 1740, homes, warehouses, stores, workshops, and taverns began to dot Norfolk\'s streets.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk was burned down during the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       . After the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        Revolution\n       </a>\n       , Norfolk was rebuilt in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_architecture" title="Federal architecture">\n        Federal\n       </a>\n       style, based on Roman ideals. Federal-style homes kept Georgian symmetry, though they had more refined decorations to look like\n       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">\n        New World\n       </a>\n       homes. Federal homes had features such as narrow sidelights with an embracing\n       <a href="/wiki/Fanlight" title="Fanlight">\n        fanlight\n       </a>\n       around the doorway, giant porticoes, gable or flat roofs, and projecting bays on exterior walls. Rooms were oval, elliptical or octagonal. Few of these federal\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rowhouse" title="Rowhouse">\n        rowhouses\n       </a>\n       remain standing today. A majority of buildings were made of wood and had a simple construction.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the early nineteenth century,\n       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">\n        Neoclassical\n       </a>\n       architectural elements began to appear in the federal style row homes, such as iconic\n       <a href="/wiki/Classical_order" title="Classical order">\n        columns\n       </a>\n       in the porticoes and classic motifs over doorways and windows. Many Federal-style row houses were modernized by placing a Greek-style porch at the front. Greek and Roman elements were integrated into public buildings such as the old City Hall, the old Norfolk Academy, and the Customs House.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="689" data-file-width="977" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg/175px-Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg/263px-Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg/350px-Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Whittle_House_Norfolk.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Taylor-Whittle_House" title="Taylor-Whittle House">\n          Taylor-Whittle House\n         </a>\n         (c. 1790), now occupied by the Junior League of Norfolk-Virginia Beach and the Norfolk Historical Society\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n          <a href="#cite_note-32">\n           [32]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Greek-style homes gave way to\n       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">\n        Gothic Revival\n       </a>\n       in the 1830s, which emphasized\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pointed_arch" title="Pointed arch">\n        pointed arches\n       </a>\n       , steep\n       <a href="/wiki/Gable" title="Gable">\n        gable\n       </a>\n       roofs, towers and tracer-lead windows. The Freemason Baptist Church and St. Mary\'s Catholic Church are examples of Gothic Revival.\n       <a href="/wiki/Italianate_architecture" title="Italianate architecture">\n        Italianate\n       </a>\n       elements emerged in the 1840s including\n       <a href="/wiki/Cupola" title="Cupola">\n        cupolas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Veranda" title="Veranda">\n        verandas\n       </a>\n       , ornamental\n       <a href="/wiki/Brickwork" title="Brickwork">\n        brickwork\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quoin_(architecture)" title="Quoin (architecture)">\n        corner quoins\n       </a>\n       . Norfolk still had simple wooden structures among its more ornate buildings.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-rise" title="High-rise">\n        High-rise\n       </a>\n       buildings were first built in the late nineteenth century when structures such as the current Commodore Maury Hotel and the Royster Building were constructed to form the initial Norfolk skyline. Past styles were revived during the early years of the 20th century. Bungalows and apartment buildings became popular for those living in the city.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       wore on,\n       <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">\n        Art Deco\n       </a>\n       emerged as a popular building style, as evidenced by the Post Office building downtown. Art Deco consisted of streamlined\n       <a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">\n        concrete\n       </a>\n       faced appearance with smooth\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_(geology)" title="Rock (geology)">\n        stone\n       </a>\n       or metal, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Terracotta" title="Terracotta">\n        terracotta\n       </a>\n       , and trimming consisting of\n       <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">\n        glass\n       </a>\n       and colored\n       <a href="/wiki/Tile" title="Tile">\n        tiles\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Neighborhoods">\n        Neighborhoods\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Neighborhoods">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_neighborhoods_in_Norfolk" title="List of neighborhoods in Norfolk">\n        List of neighborhoods in Norfolk\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk has a variety of historic neighborhoods. Some neighborhoods, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkley,_Virginia" title="Berkley, Virginia">\n        Berkley\n       </a>\n       , were formerly cities and towns. Others, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Willoughby_Spit" title="Willoughby Spit">\n        Willoughby Spit\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ocean_View,_Virginia" title="Ocean View, Virginia">\n        Ocean View\n       </a>\n       , have a long history tied to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       . Today, neighborhoods such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Downtown Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Downtown\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghent_district" title="Ghent district">\n        Ghent\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fairmount_Park_Neighborhood" title="Fairmount Park Neighborhood">\n        Fairmount Park\n       </a>\n       have transformed with the revitalization that the city has undergone.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Norfolk,_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Norfolk has a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       with moderate changes of seasons. Spring arrives in March with mild days and cool nights, and by late May, the temperature has warmed up considerably to herald warm summer days. Summers are consistently warm and humid, but the nearby Atlantic Ocean often exercises a slight cooling effect on daytime high temperatures, but a slight warming effect on nighttime low temperatures (compared to areas farther inland). As such, Norfolk has occasional days over 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). Temperatures over 100 F. are rare but can occur on occasion. On average, July is the warmest month, and August is the year\'s wettest month, due to still-frequent summer thunderstorm activity combined with a rising frequency (in August) of tropical activity (hurricanes and tropical storms), which can bring high winds and heavy rains. These usually brush Norfolk and only occasionally make landfalls in the area; the highest-risk period is mid-August to the end of September.\n       <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">\n        Fall\n       </a>\n       is marked by mild to warm days and cooler nights. Winter is usually mild in Norfolk, with average winter days featuring lows near or slightly above freezing and highs in the upper-40s to mid-50s (8 to 13\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C). On average, the coldest month of the year is January. Norfolk\'s record high was 105\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (41\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on August 7, 1918, and July 24 and 25, 2010, and the record low was \xe2\x88\x923\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9219\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) recorded on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/January_1985_Arctic_outbreak" title="January 1985 Arctic outbreak">\n        January 21, 1985\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TWC-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Snow occurs sporadically, with an average annual accumulation of 5.8 inches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <br/>\n
